        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer983933275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5306660322811129341">A nice, well-executed novel. I wanted to read this because I've always loved books with natural powers such as earth, water, wind and fire. They fascinate me. <br/><br/>'Storm' began with action and suspense and I liked that but somewhere along the way it lost its edge. Maybe because it was uneventful. Then it picked up and it became thrilling again and I loved the ending too, although I would have liked some closure. <br/><br/>So we have this caring, giving, kind girl named Becca who's always been one to have eyes</span>
  <span id="freeText5306660322811129341" style="display:none">A nice, well-executed novel. I wanted to read this because I've always loved books with natural powers such as earth, water, wind and fire. They fascinate me. <br /><br />'Storm' began with action and suspense and I liked that but somewhere along the way it lost its edge. Maybe because it was uneventful. Then it picked up and it became thrilling again and I loved the ending too, although I would have liked some closure. <br /><br />So we have this caring, giving, kind girl named Becca who's always been one to have eyes drawn on her, not because she provoked people around her or anything like that. It's just the way it is. People always picked on Becca. Living with her mother after her father abandoned them, her childhood has not been easy. But she's grown to become an amazing person.<br /><br />Then one night she saves Chris Merrick from a beating and her life unexpectedly becomes intertwined with the Merrick brothers. Soon, she discovers that they have powers. Earth, water, fire and wind. And the fifth one: spirit. As the book progresses Becca always finds herself either saving or being saved by the Merrick brothers, and more particularly, Chris. The amazing Chris, protective, I'd describe as a wallflower although he's not afraid to stand up to anything, he mostly keeps to himself, which is why I loved the dude.<br /><br />Then there is Hunter, the enigmatic, mysterious new guy at school, who swoops in and steals Becca from Chris (I may be biased on that one, so). <br /><br />I liked the plot, I would have liked it if it had been a little thicker but there's always the next book. Was this book good? Yes, I'm totally recommending it (nice ya right here). Is there room for improvement? Hell, I'm already sure the next book is going to rock my world. Why did it I give it 3 stars? I'm saving my 4 and 5 for the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5306660322811129341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

</a><br><br>And because of that power, the other Elementals feared them and are set on eliminate them. Only a truce made some years ago, stays between them and the ones that want them gone. However, that don't stop the other of bullying them, beat them up, trying to make them lose control, to break the curse and force the Guides, to come and "deal" with the situation.<br><br>Becca know nothing of this "world" and one night when she sees 2 guys beating up Chris, she goes for it and saves him. And that just made her into the hit list, alongside Chris and his brothers.<br><br>Now with Hunter, the new kid, antagonizing Kris and trying to win her affection, she must discover which one of them has a hold in her heart and which one isn't telling the whole truth....<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/839/tumblrm8m0o64knx1rrhz69.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380408726ra/799806.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I'm LOVING this series!<br>It's quite a refreshing story in the paranormal genre and it's quite awesome, to see how they can control or try to control their elements. <br>And especially how each personality match so well their element.<br><br><b>
  <i> His affinity to water made sense. He reminded her of the sea, alluring and mysterious, calm on the surface, with who-knew-what brewing underneath.</i>
</b><br><br>Besides all the action packed scenes (and they're are amazing and nerve-wrecking), the story has dept,angst,it's witty and overall such a GREAT read. It's easy to connect with them and of course to root for them.<br><br><b>
  <i> 4.5 stars </i>
</b><br><br>For this one and more reviews go to:<br><a href="http://neverendingbookconfessions.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener"> A Bookworm Confessions </a></span>

<div id="review_630863335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630863335" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630863335?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758280053" href="/book/show/13614844-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=paranormal-fantasy">paranormal-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630863335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1251829831446920553"><a href='http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/lightningstorm_zps871934ee.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387423325i/7594754._SY540_.png' alt=' photo lightningstorm_zps871934ee.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Wow, I haven’t felt this way while reading a book in quite awhile! That feeling that your eyes just can’t move fast enough across the pages to eat up the words. That even when you are not reading, your mind is still on the characters. That your heartbeat is going a little bit too fast. I didn’t even take the time to highlight anything. So this review won’t have any quotes in it. Sorry about that!<br/><br/>In <i>Storm</i> we meet the youngest Merrick brother, Chris. Chris gets his power from water. And, we me</span>
  <span id="freeText1251829831446920553" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/lightningstorm_zps871934ee.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1387423325i/7594754._SY540_.png" alt=" photo lightningstorm_zps871934ee.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Wow, I haven’t felt this way while reading a book in quite awhile! That feeling that your eyes just can’t move fast enough across the pages to eat up the words. That even when you are not reading, your mind is still on the characters. That your heartbeat is going a little bit too fast. I didn’t even take the time to highlight anything. So this review won’t have any quotes in it. Sorry about that!<br><br>In <i>Storm</i> we meet the youngest Merrick brother, Chris. Chris gets his power from water. And, we meet Becca Chandler. She is Chris’s age. Becca lives with her mother but her father left years ago. She never knew why. Becca knows nothing of the world of Elementals but one night after attending a self defense class at the high school, while going to her car she witnesses Seth and Tyler beating up Chris. She is scared to death but she can’t just let them beat him, so she saves him. After involving herself with the Merrick family, she is then mistakenly identified as being one of them and this puts her in danger. <br><br>About the same time, there is a new boy at school, Hunter. There is an instant attraction between Becca and Hunter but he has secrets of his own. She wants to trust him, but can she? Then tensions build between Chris and Hunter and she doesn’t know who she should trust! If all of this wasn’t enough for Becca to handle, out of the blue her father shows up and tries to get back into her life.<br><br>This book is non-stop all the way through. You are fully involved from the first page until the last page. The characters are all so relatable. You don’t know who to trust. They all have stories of their own that pull at your heart strings so you don’t want any of them to be bad. Except Seth and Tyler. I don’t think there is ANYTHING good about them. In this book I was so proud of Becca. Even with all she was given to cope with, she was strong. Her moral compass never wavered. These Merrick boys are already securely implanted in my heart and I can’t wait to read the next book. All I can say to the author, Brigid Kemmerer is: You…Are…Awesome!!!<br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_325930726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325930726" />
    <a title="Zuleeza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4883387-zuleeza"><img alt="Zuleeza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392172290p2/4883387.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/325930726?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zuleeza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zuleeza" href="/user/show/4883387-zuleeza">Zuleeza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer325930726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15362865716049355697">This review is also available on my blog, <a href='http://zue-leysza.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Qwerty</a><br/><br/>Okay, it's a challenge to write a review after half a month I finished with this book. Ha-ha! It's what you got when you chose to read a book right before a major exam starts.<br/><br/>One thing I vividly remember though...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380377176i/732424.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This book haz it.<br/><br/>Where do I begin...how about THE FIVE HOT GUYS! (Actually, Becca's dad was actually kind of cute until I actually found out his secret).<br/><br/>Well, it didn't reach the point where I found my ovaries were exploding. But, close en</span>
  <span id="freeText15362865716049355697" style="display:none">This review is also available on my blog, <a href="http://zue-leysza.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Qwerty</a><br><br>Okay, it's a challenge to write a review after half a month I finished with this book. Ha-ha! It's what you got when you chose to read a book right before a major exam starts.<br><br>One thing I vividly remember though...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380377176i/732424.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This book haz it.<br><br>Where do I begin...how about THE FIVE HOT GUYS! (Actually, Becca's dad was actually kind of cute until I actually found out his secret).<br><br>Well, it didn't reach the point where I found my ovaries were exploding. But, close enough nonetheless. No matter what kind of guys you like, you're in for a ride.<br><br>Micheal, the eldest is the father-figure in the bunch. He is protective (overly-protective sometimes) and responsible. If you can ignore his distant and cold aura, that is.<br><br>Gabriel, one of the twins is the mini Tony Stark. Genius, billionaire, playboy, philantrophist. Oh wait, minus the genius part. <br><br>And the billionaire part.<br><br>And...and the philantrophist part too.<br><br>Hurmm...I guess Gabriel is not the mini Tony Stark.<br><br>He's more like the Human Torch from Fantastic Four, I think. (Oh, Chris Evans! Squeeeeee)<br><br>Nicholas!!! The other twin. <i>Don't you dare call him Nicky!</i> It's not even cute. He's my favourite because I aways drawn to nice, nerdy, intelligent guys. With a sense of humour, of course. (Now you know why I remain single, don't you? Haha). <br><br>And why? WHY??? Nicholas can't have a book for himself, Brigid Kemmerer? WHY???!!!<br><br>And lastly, Chris is the focus of this book. His insecurity makes him such a douche sometimes. But overall, he is this sweet and sensitive guy.<br><br>Huh? I totally forgot about Hunter. He is cool, I guess but generally I just don't like blond guys? (Maybe I deserve to be stoned to death for my discrimination but I can't help it!). Believe it or not, he was the one guy who almost managed to get my ovaries to explode. I almost wanted to shove Becca away from Hunter's embrace and whisper "Take me instead, Hunter! I'd wear all those crazy bracelets you have in your possession though I'm not a hippie". Note that I have nothing against hippies.<br><br>Sheesh, this review is going nowhere.<br><br>ANYWAY, with so many male characters interacting at one time, it was hard for me to exactly pinpoint who is this 'he' and 'him'. <br><br>Next, plotwise, this book was going at slowpoke level. I mean, really half of the book had been summarized in the blurb already. I had this "You're so dumb, Becca. Of course, they are Elementals. It's written at the back cover of the book!" moment. But she couldn't possibly know this. Oh, well.<br><br>Again, plotwise, the initial chapters are dedicated to one after another testosterone-fueled brawls between the guys and I thought<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380377176i/732425._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It didn't help with the fact that I was forced to read what colour Chris' and Gabriel's shirts are and whether Micheal is wearing any slippers or not. God, Becca, the guys are hot I get it, but no need to be overly observant. This kind of writing made Becca looks cheap.<br><br>Okay, with so many low points you must be wondering, WHY DID I GIVE THIS FREAKING BOOK FOUR STARS ANYWAY?<br><br>It was because of the FUN! It amazed me how closely the dialogues sound like everyday teenage conversations. I actually laughed numerous times due to the guys' snide remarks and Becca's dramatic monologues. Me. Laughing. The stoic me who hardly laugh at jokes.<br><br>Quite an achievement, I must say Ms Kemmerer.<br><br>But then again, this book is not something I would want my dad to know about because if he found out I'm reading this kind of books, he would bury me alive and seal my coffin shut with adamantium nails.<br><br>Why? Because the level of cursing caused me headache at some points. <br><br>But my dad is not on GR! So hoorrahhh!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15362865716049355697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_322426245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/322426245" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/322426245?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer322426245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10260387809268171455"><br/>After all the glowing reviews for Storm, I was a little afraid that it may not live up to my expectations. Looks like I didn't need to worry! <br/><br/>Let's just get this confession out of the way: I heard "<b>four hot boys</b>" and I just <i>knew</i> I had to read this. The four we're talking about are the Merrick brothers, born with special elemental abilities, able to draw up power and control the forces of nature. Each brother has a specialization: air, fire, water, earth (and yes, they are all HOT!). Because of t</span>
  <span id="freeText10260387809268171455" style="display:none"><br />After all the glowing reviews for Storm, I was a little afraid that it may not live up to my expectations. Looks like I didn't need to worry! <br /><br />Let's just get this confession out of the way: I heard "<b>four hot boys</b>" and I just <i>knew</i> I had to read this. The four we're talking about are the Merrick brothers, born with special elemental abilities, able to draw up power and control the forces of nature. Each brother has a specialization: air, fire, water, earth (and yes, they are all HOT!). Because of their exceptionally strong powers, the Merrick's are viewed as a potential threat. Technically, they should be reported and killed, but the Merrick's parents made a deal long ago to keep them safe, as long as they don't use their powers. This has made them the subject of constant bullying because the neighbors in the community who know of their abilities are fearful and envious. Also, they know they can do whatever they want without the brothers fighting back. But this is about to change. <br /><br />This installment focuses on Chris Merrick, the youngest of the brothers, and Becca, a girl in his school. These two are thrust together after Becca comes to the aid of Chris, who was being attacked by these cruel bullies. She scares them off, and in the process, becomes a target as well. Becca has had her own problems with these bullies after her ex-boyfriend spread some nasty rumors to the whole school about her. She just wants the situation to go away, but her intentions of lying low are ruined after helping Chris. The enemies of the Merrick's feel she must either be an elemental also, or she's on their side. Either way, she's in the middle. At first, Becca is far from being on their side. When she takes the battered Chris home, she gets nothing but flack from Michael, the oldest brother and guardian of the brothers. She plans on washing her hands of all those surly and ungrateful men! Unfortunately, circumstances continually throw them together. Added to the mix is the <i>mysterious</i> new guy, Hunter (yes, he's hot too!), who shows up at school, intent on getting close to Becca. Hmm….<br /><br />This story read like an action/adventure movie, a non-stop thrill ride. If I had more time, I could've easily sat down and read this in one sitting. It's one of those stories where you want to keep turning the page to find out what happens next. I loved all these brothers, and it was fun to see Becca deal with them and stand up to their teasing and snarky remarks. She definitely wasn't a pushover. Here's a fun quote:<br /><br /><b><i>Gabriel: "Finding a girl in the kitchen isn't exactly and oddity around here." Becca: "Charming." He glanced up at that, a glint of wicked humor in his eye. "I'm sure </i>you're<i> special, though." It should have pissed her off, after Michael's brusque attitude and Nick's hey-baby-why-don't-you-come-inside. But Gabriel's teasing was straightforward, challenging, in a way. He expected her to girl it up, to huff and fold her arms. She could tell. "Not special at all.----I just heard my number called and thought I better show up."</i></b><br /> <br />I loved the gradual build between Chris and Becca. I wasn't really thrilled with her getting close to Hunter because I'm not a fan of love-triangles but this one wasn't too frustrating. <br /><br />This story was a <i>little</i> on the predictable side, but even so, it was very entertaining. I guess we get a short story with Hunter in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13503581.Fearless__Elemental___1_5_" title="Fearless (Elemental, #1.5) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Fearless</a>, and then Gabriel's story in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12977172.Spark__Elemental___2_" title="Spark (Elemental, #2) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Spark</a>. Can’t wait! <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://www.thereadersden.blogspot.com/2012/06/review-storm-by-brigid-kemmerer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10260387809268171455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_297593318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297593318" />
    <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda"><img alt="Jessica Buwalda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600119200p2/6926261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297593318?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Buwalda" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda">Jessica Buwalda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6926261-jessica-buwalda?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297593318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6118750133838341499">Oh my giddy-aunt I love this book! This is the sort of book that you crawl into the corner of the couch with, pull up your legs and bring all your limbs as close together as possible, then commence drumming your fingers against your bottom lip while you smile like you have some hidden secret. No really…I did that at one point. I also gasped out loud (a lot), smiled, giggled, and clapped multiple times while reading this book. I may have also hit a dear friend that was sitting beside me while I w</span>
  <span id="freeText6118750133838341499" style="display:none">Oh my giddy-aunt I love this book! This is the sort of book that you crawl into the corner of the couch with, pull up your legs and bring all your limbs as close together as possible, then commence drumming your fingers against your bottom lip while you smile like you have some hidden secret. No really…I did that at one point. I also gasped out loud (a lot), smiled, giggled, and clapped multiple times while reading this book. I may have also hit a dear friend that was sitting beside me while I was reading this book out of pure joy. It should come with a warning: “The happiness resulting from this book may cause irrational violence”. Sort of like the warning when you’re about to play a Wii game about needing to stand so far away.<br />Let me break it down for you: 5 hot guys, one girl. 1-girl who saves 1-guy from getting the crap kicked out of him and delivers him to his brothers, including 1-scary older over protective ass-hat of a brothers and 2-(twins) that get into a lot of mischief and sure as hell know how to work their way around some great sarcasm and comebacks, then throw in 1-goth/rebel like guy who happens to wear a lot of jewellery and who, within 30 seconds of meeting said girl, make this girl swoon because of his Krav Maga hotness, and who sort of gets on the nerve of guy #1 who happens to also not be able to get girl #1 out of his head. Throw in some daddy issues and one seriously bad choice that happened 6 weeks ago and you have a stew for greatness. Intimidating at first with its close to 400 pages (over 400 with the novella and sneak peek) and small writing I actually set this book aside and started on another book before I finally stepped up to the plate and picked this bad boy up. Lets just say I had no reason to be scared. I was ensnarled with this book from about page…oh….2. I’m not 100% sure how to describe it other than all the teen angst, teen insecurity, sarcasm, wit, banter, and sexy boys just made this into a book that is definitely going to be sitting on my stop shelf (where all my absolute favourites are). I cannot wait for the next in the series. No seriously…I can’t I’ve already pre-purchased it via The Book Depository.<br /><br />Good:<br /><br />Becca: Brave, yet scared too. But that doesn’t stop her.<br /><br />Chris Merrick: If he looks anything like he does on the cover he is extremely hot. But apparently all the Merrick boys are, as the throw around extremely heavy top spoil bags for a living…it must define a lot of muscles. Not to mention he thinks only about Becca and how all he wants to do is wrap her in his arms. Then he goes and does something like sticks up for her and gets detention because of it and I was sold.<br /><br />Gabriel Merrick: obviously the seriously mad boy out of the bunch (I say seriously because they all tend to be a little bad) who knows that he looks good and loves to flaunt it. Also the sportive one of the bunch who uses the fact that he and his brother are identical to his benefit (i.e be on two varsity soccer teams at once under different names). Ouuuu!!!…shame on you Gabriel. You sexy thing.<br /><br />Nicolas Merrick: apparently the genius and light headed one of the family. That is saying a lot considering he is generally found right along side his brother pulling some decent pranks and razzing their younger brother Chris.<br /><br />Michael Merrick: Although the pony tail threw me a bit it was his ass-hatness that threw me even more but in the end Michael Merrick was seen as just as tough and hot as his brothers through my eyes.<br /><br />Hunter: obviously the sexiest rebel like child we’ve ever seen. Swift, strong, and a deep down nice guy. If that didn’t get you then his dog Casper sure will.<br /><br />Bad: <br /><br />So…I thought and thought about what I would put here and I guess there was only one thing to do with the book. In the beginning I loved Chris, somewhere in the middle not so much, then in the end I loved him again. Perhaps it was what Kemmerer was going for? For us to mirror good old Becky’s feelings? Well all and all there should have been more Chris and Becca…mainly them making out…but there are more books to come so you never know. *Fingers crossed<br /><br />Overall (Writing style, story line, and general):<br /><br />Overall I love Brigid Kemmerer. Her being a new writer I wasn’t sure what to expect, but then when the reviews kept rolling in and I didn’t see anything other than a 5/5 I had to see what she was all about. Her writing style is beautiful. Its not confusing and like so many others she bring her humour across beautifully. But I think the shocker is that she can do it with so many characters…so many male characters especially. The book was paced perfectly with action around ever corner and the meaningful reflective moments and romantic moments exactly where it felt they should be. This series is one that will be highly loved for readers across the world.<br />So I’ve looked forward and into the other books in the series and I am delighted to see that the next one in the series is all about Gabriel, and of course the novella “Elemental” is all about Michael, this one, Storm, is all about Chris, but then I was surprised to see the third one will be about Hunter. Um….what happened to Nicky? Come on there has to be a Nick book. P.s. Nick and Quinn…oh ya its going to happen.<br /><br />View more of my review and others at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com">www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6118750133838341499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1120775943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1120775943" />
    <a title="Nadia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25547640-nadia"><img alt="Nadia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587020307p2/25547640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1120775943?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadia" href="/user/show/25547640-nadia">Nadia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=eyes-are-rolling-and-face-is-palmed">eyes-are-rolling-and-face-is-palmed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=annoying-side-characters">annoying-side-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=i-wanna-punch-the-hero-in-the-face">i-wanna-punch-the-hero-in-the-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=dumb-dumber-the-heroine">dumb-dumber-the-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=cheesy-attacks">cheesy-attacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=i-m-so-mad">i-m-so-mad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25547640-nadia?shelf=stupid">stupid</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1120775943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13118872368198739667"><b>This book drove me nuts. And I'm in the mood to rant.</b> <br/>You wanna know why? Because idiotic heroine, obnoxious heroes, fucking love triangle, teenage drama. <br/><br/>I'm too old for this shit.<br/><br/>I'm trying really hard to write a coherent review, but every time I think of anything from that list above, I start to see red. <br/><br/>I'll begin from Becca, because she is what made this book insufferable for me. Becca has the personality of a kitchen cloth, which is my witty way of saying she has none. Nothing makes her sp</span>
  <span id="freeText13118872368198739667" style="display:none"><b>This book drove me nuts. And I'm in the mood to rant.</b> <br />You wanna know why? Because idiotic heroine, obnoxious heroes, fucking love triangle, teenage drama. <br /><br />I'm too old for this shit.<br /><br />I'm trying really hard to write a coherent review, but every time I think of anything from that list above, I start to see red. <br /><br />I'll begin from Becca, because she is what made this book insufferable for me. Becca has the personality of a kitchen cloth, which is my witty way of saying she has none. Nothing makes her special or stand out from every other girl. Is she exceptionally smart? Hahahhaha, no. Is she stunningly beautiful? Meh. Is she in any other way interesting, maybe cunning or charismatic, strong, brave, daring, anything, just to prove she's a worthy heroine? Nope. <br />So you see, a cloth is a perfect comparison for her personality. <br />No, I'm not being fair when I say she has no significant talents. She has one talent. When shit starts to hit the fan, Becca can get in the middle like nobody's business. Every single time things start to go downhill, she manages to get involved and end up in a life threatening situation, only so she could be rescued by the heroes. *facepalms herself into eternity* God forbid she has the presence of mind to get herself out of difficult situations. *facepalms herself into eternity the second time*<br /><br />Aaaand the blushing! Oh my god, the blushing!! Fine, once or twice I can understand, but every freaking time she talks to someone she blushes! At this point it's past shyness and social awkwardness, this is a physical condition that should be medically treated! Maybe it's like a high blood pressure thing or whatever. That much blushing and flushing couldn't be healthy, for real.<br /><br />What's next on my list? Obnoxious heroes. As it is in YA, they're all really not boys anymore (as sixteen-year-olds still tend to be) but they're all like really grown up with defined cheekbones and jawlines and muscles and voices and each one is basically sex on a stick, just perfect human beings with no flaws at all. You can't beat them, you can't fluster them, you can't do them wrong. <br />A conversation between a perfect Hunter and the oh-so-plain Becca is TORTURE! <br /><br />And fuck me if that love triangle made any sense! And how it was resolved. Ugh. No sense. <br /><br />I'll cut this review short before I start repeating random words for "emphasis". It's no secret I didn't like this book. But, I'll read the next one. Why? Because I'm a glutton for punishment. Just kidding, I'm not, but I'm feeling patient and maybe the next book proves to be better. I keep hoping this might be like the <i>Fever</i> series, where you have to suffer through the first book to get to the awesomeness that is the rest of the series. So, off to the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13118872368198739667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1745794458" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745794458" />
    <a title="eleni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41185165-eleni"><img alt="eleni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502125432p2/41185165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745794458?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="eleni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="eleni" href="/user/show/41185165-eleni">eleni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41185165-eleni?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41185165-eleni?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41185165-eleni?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41185165-eleni?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745794458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10234121559171436992">“I haven't gotten in a fight yet this year!<br/>Despite everything, that made her smile. "It's September."<br/>He waved a hand. "Details.” <br/><br/> So, i'm going to try to write my first ever detailed review of a book because i loved this one so much!<br/><br/> Storm is about a girl, named Becca, who saves a boy, named Chris, when she sees him getting beaten up by two strangers! Then, she gets tangled up in his family story, as she discovers that Chris and his three brothers have special powers according to their element (</span>
  <span id="freeText10234121559171436992" style="display:none">“I haven't gotten in a fight yet this year!<br />Despite everything, that made her smile. "It's September."<br />He waved a hand. "Details.” <br /><br /> So, i'm going to try to write my first ever detailed review of a book because i loved this one so much!<br /><br /> Storm is about a girl, named Becca, who saves a boy, named Chris, when she sees him getting beaten up by two strangers! Then, she gets tangled up in his family story, as she discovers that Chris and his three brothers have special powers according to their element (earth, fire, wind, water). Now she has to find her way out of this mess and try to help the Merrick brothers while sorting out her personal life!<br /><br /> The plot was great and one crazy thing happened after another! But what really got me were the characters. Each character was complicated and had their own tragic story. Michael, who is the oldest of the four, had to carry the weight of the family and take care of his brothers, after their parents died, and Gabriel was certainly not making it easy for him! His brothers had isolated him and blamed him for everything. The twins had the best sibling relationship, I think. They always understood each other and helped each other. I always feel that twins have a special bond that nobody can break. Gabriel was the 'bad boy', whereas Nick was the sweet, caring one. Finally, Chris was like a confused puppy. He had to learn to control his powers and tried to put up a tough front, but in reality he was vulnerable and lonely! Becca was a great female lead. She was strong and always tried to do the best thing for everyone even though she had been hurt by people in the past. As for the minor characters, Quinn was a bit abrasive and loud mouthed but it was only because she cared so much about her loved ones and Hunter was a character-mystery for me as i feel that there was a deeper meaning behind his every word.<br /> The romance was quite strong in this one and there was a love triangle but i didn't feel that it overpowered the story at any point. I hope this was not the last time we see Becca and Chris because they are so sweet and young and innocent and i love them!<br /> The only thing that I didn't like was the fact that a couple of times women were judged because of the way they dressed. Also, I don't think Becca stopped blushing throughout the entire story.<br /> Overall, I loved it and I can't wait to continue with the series. Unfortunately, I have a full tbr for September, so Spark I'll see you next month! &lt;3 &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="10234121559171436992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2012">best-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=finished-copy-for-review">finished-copy-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=authors-i-want-to-meet">authors-i-want-to-meet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260346271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2971703767031258910">I was pressured, brainwashed, and totally convinced to go into this book with high expectations, and even then it still blew me away! So. Darn. AMAZING!<br/><br/><b>Storm</b> starts on a dark night when our awesome heroine Becca literally saves Chris Merrick's life. Everything quickly goes to hell from there when she realizes that Chris and his brothers aren't normal — they're Elementals, targeted because of how powerful they are. And now that she knows the truth, Becca isn't so safe either.<br/><br/>Becca is the perfect </span>
  <span id="freeText2971703767031258910" style="display:none">I was pressured, brainwashed, and totally convinced to go into this book with high expectations, and even then it still blew me away! So. Darn. AMAZING!<br /><br /><b>Storm</b> starts on a dark night when our awesome heroine Becca literally saves Chris Merrick's life. Everything quickly goes to hell from there when she realizes that Chris and his brothers aren't normal — they're Elementals, targeted because of how powerful they are. And now that she knows the truth, Becca isn't so safe either.<br /><br />Becca is the perfect imperfect heroine for this novel! She's bad-ass and tough, but she's also vulnerable in a way that makes her so <i>real</i>. One thing I loved about this book was how Brigid Kemmerer incorporated bullying into the mix — with Becca's ex-boyfriend (who I hate with a passion!) spreading awful rumors about her. She reacts to it the way most girls would, and I couldn't have loved her more if I tried.<br /><br />This review would not be completely without mentioning the <u>Merrick brothers</u>. ♥ There's <b>Michael</b>, the oldest who controls earth; <b>Gabriel</b>, the super-hot twin who ironically controls fire; <b>Nick</b>, the sweeter air-controlling twin who is no less hot; and then there's <b>Chris</b>, the youngest, the water-controller, the main character of this novel, and my favourite so far!<br /><br />As one of my friends said, you'd think Brigid Kemmerer grew up in a house full of boys with how well she wrote them! Their brotherly bond, the way they fought, their heated banter... Topped off with Brigid's great writing and the sweet romance, this book has it all.<br /><br />With four hot brothers, a fantastic heroine, an Elemental-based storyline that will steal your breath away, <b>Storm</b> was one of my most highly anticipated reads of the year and it definitely lives up to the hype! Brigid Kemmerer, you are definitely starting off on the right foot with this debut. :) I can't wait to get my hands on <b>Spark</b>, Gabriel's story, later in the fall!<br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> Hahahahahaha you're funny. Why would you even think to borrow this? Buy all the way!! :') <br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/05/review-storm.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2971703767031258910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_317385946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317385946" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317385946?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317385946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7411487068590667396">3.5 stars<br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brigid-kemmerer/review-storm.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375819i/730481.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I had my eyes on this book for a while because most of my friends have read it and loved it, so when I got a copy of Spark (the second book in the series) for review I thought that it was time for me to start reading this series too.<br/><br/>Don't be fooled by the 3 and a half star-rating, the book is quite good and if you don't usually over-think the paranormal worlds (like I seem to do) you will definitely love it more.<br/>This is a refreshing story about 4 boys with powers way too strong for </span>
  <span id="freeText7411487068590667396" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brigid-kemmerer/review-storm.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375819i/730481.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I had my eyes on this book for a while because most of my friends have read it and loved it, so when I got a copy of Spark (the second book in the series) for review I thought that it was time for me to start reading this series too.<br><br>Don't be fooled by the 3 and a half star-rating, the book is quite good and if you don't usually over-think the paranormal worlds (like I seem to do) you will definitely love it more.<br>This is a refreshing story about 4 boys with powers way too strong for their own good and also a story about a girl caught in the middle of a fight beyond her power of comprehension. This is a story about revealing secrets that could kill you and about love that could heal you, it has a lot of action, a bit a drama, some humor scattered here in there, not to mention that there is plenty of hotness involved. Be aware!<br><br>THE GOOD<br><br>The concept.<br>If I remember Captain Planet, am I a bit too old?<br>Well this book reminded me of that cartoon movie series and I've always liked the idea of one controlling the surrounding natural elements, the idea of them giving you power, the idea of that power consuming you.. Yeah, I am talking now a bit more about Chris' brothers than himself, but in this story they come all in one package and some of them will steal your heart with their humor, or their drama, or them both.<br><br>The characters.<br>When you have 5 hot guys parading (is this the right word?) in front of you, you just got to be enjoying yourself.. a lot!<br>I loved the teasing between the brothers and Chris when we started to see Becca, I loved how they stood for each other even when they disagreed with what one was doing, I loved how they wanted to fight back and not keep their head down because that wouldn't solve anything and they would be bullied again and again. Yeah, sometimes the overprotectiveness was getting on my nerves, but this is what loving your younger might do to one (I have a younger sister and I like to think that I would do everything to keep her out of trouble, even though it's not the case).<br><br>The writing.<br>The is something melodic about the way Brigid writes. It captivates you and makes you want to read more, to know more, to see what happens next.. You simply can't put the book down. I've been reading on the train, on a bus and a boat, and it's funny because i usually get motions sick if I read in a moving vehicle, but I guess that the story was way too interesting for my brain to think of something else.<br><br>THE BAD(-ish)<br><br>The fake love triangle.<br>When you have alternating povs from two main characters things are clearer than bottled water. And when you have a cute relationship that starts pretty well, but you know with whom the girl might end it leaves you with a bitter taste.<br>I am not a big fan of paranormal love stories and this one was no exception. I don't understand why did the two liked each other, and i don't understand why the third one got to be left out when he started so damn well, I don't know why there was a need for a love-triangle in the first place, and I don't get how Becca ended with the one she ended because not only there was no chemistry between them, but it was the same treat-me-like-hell-because-i-like-you story all over again.<br><br>The paranormal elements.<br>There were things that didn't make much sense, mostly by the ending. We started to understand many things, but as a paranormal world goes it wasn't really enough.<br>Making storms out of nothings is something, but changing the course of life is an entirely different thing, and no-one seemed to be bothered by this. (And the same goes for the next book and there are still no consequences!)<br><br>The confession.<br>Again with these paranormal clichés. You can't just go tell a girl all your secrets only because you like her and she knows a bit of it anyways. There are sectrets that are not only yours, the are things more powerful than you, there are sectrets that could kill.<br><br>Also there were some disturbing things left hanging... Again, i know this is paranormal fantasy, but young people are reading it. Don't make them think that if someone tries to rape you is alright for you to hide it. Make them fucking pay for it! It really annoys me that something this important is treated so lightly in YA books.<br><br>CONCLUSION<br><br>With the good and the bad, I really got to like the story, enough for me to want to read the next ones (I am including here Spark that comes next this month and also Elemental, a short story about the oldest brother). Keep an eye for this series because I bet that many of you will like it as well!<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brigid-kemmerer/review-storm.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696540.jpg" alt="" width="483" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> ** This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/brigid-kemmerer/review-storm.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

<div id="review_309711833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309711833" />
    <a title="Sarah (saz101)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3825460-sarah-saz101"><img alt="Sarah (saz101)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300234087p2/3825460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309711833?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah (saz101)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah (saz101)" href="/user/show/3825460-sarah-saz101">Sarah (saz101)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743310663" href="/book/show/12381271-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3825460-sarah-saz101?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309711833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5481247550238284916">Four brothers, each a powerful elemental, a community at war, and one girl caught in the middle, Brigid Kemmerer brings her A-game in her electrifying debut. Storm should come with a cautionary notice. Something like: <em>“Severe Weather Warning: This book will </em>blow<em> you away.”</em><br/><br/><strong>The Story: </strong><br/>When Becca Chandler saves a boy from a brutal beating in her school’s parking lot, chasing off his attackers, she has no idea what her good Samaritan act is getting her caught up in. The boy is Chris Merrick, who, al</span>
  <span id="freeText5481247550238284916" style="display:none">Four brothers, each a powerful elemental, a community at war, and one girl caught in the middle, Brigid Kemmerer brings her A-game in her electrifying debut. Storm should come with a cautionary notice. Something like: <em>“Severe Weather Warning: This book will </em>blow<em> you away.”</em><br /><br /><strong>The Story: </strong><br />When Becca Chandler saves a boy from a brutal beating in her school’s parking lot, chasing off his attackers, she has no idea what her good Samaritan act is getting her caught up in. The boy is Chris Merrick, who, along with his brothers, is an Elemental, ‘gifted’ with the ability to control water. And that might just be the least of the surprises coming her way. It’s not only Chris’ attackers, or Chris himself, who are interested in Becca. ‘New Kid’ at school, Hunter, has his eyes on Becca, and he’s not so bad to eye back... but who should she trust? Like it or not, Becca finds herself caught up in war not just for the Merricks’ survival, but her own.<br /><br /><strong>Becca and Chris, Chris and Becca...</strong><br />Storm wastes no time jumping straight into the action. We join Becca as she finds Chris being beaten in the school parking lot, and it escalates from there. Told between Becca and Chris’ point of view, we’re give a unique viewpoint into their world: the ‘outsider’ view of Becca, as she tries to discover what she’s been dragged into, and that of Chris, who knows what’s happening around him, but still doesn’t necessarily hold all the cards or information. Both Chris and Becca are eminently likeable, fascinating and engrossing, and both have unique, singular voices.<br /><br />Becca’s not an ‘action chick’ exactly, but she’s never afraid to take action. She’s brave, curious and compassionate. After saving Chris, who is in her grade, but she hardly knows, her world is irrevocably shaken, and only gets more complicated from there. But Becca’s life is hardly simple to begin with. It becomes clear Becca has secrets of her own, and there’s a meaningful subplot to Storm in the shape of some truly vicious bullying. And this is why it’s so difficult to discuss this book. It’s not a linear love story, a paranormal, or an action-packed thriller. It’s all of these things, and it’s much more. It’s layered and nuanced in a way that renders it not just compulsively readable, but truly memorable.<br /><br />It’s not only Becca who is the victim of malicious harassment; the ‘bullying’ Chris Merrick endures could cost him his life. The quietest and most reserved of his brothers, Chris is much like element he controls: calm and still on the surface—sometimes—but hiding a tumult of dangers, currents and fathomless depths below. Watching Becca and Chris step around each other is a delight. There’s an almost palpable tension between them. The two are drawn to each other, but neither understands the other, neither knows what it means. Both hide secrets and hurts, and are struggling to fight inner demons as well as the external kind. But Storm isn’t entirely Chris and Becca’s story, there is another boy very much involved, in the way of Hunter, ‘New Kid’ at school. He’s fascinating, mysterious, and he has a story as heartbreaking, intriguing and important as Chris or Becca’s. He plays a large and important role in Storm, and it feels as though his part may only just be becoming clear.<br /><br /><strong>The Brothers</strong><br />Where Storm truly shines is in the authenticity of its characters, in particular the four brothers at its core. There’s been a lot of buzz about how ‘swoon worthy’, hot, and amazing these boys are, and it does bear repeating. But this isn’t what gives the book its compulsively readable quality, or what makes it so utterly gripping. Every one of the four Merrick boys feels real. It’s the brotherly bond they share, the care, the tension, the anger and the banter between them that is so entertaining, and at times heartbreaking, to read. Chris and his brothers are fascinating to say the least. Enormously powerful, the boys are a natural disaster waiting to happen—literally. But they keep their powers constantly tamped down. They live in fear of a power greater than theirs, creating a fascinating dichotomy between their power, and powerlessness to defend themselves without bringing a fate worse than harassment down on their heads.<br /><br /><strong>The Verdict: </strong><br />There’s a surprising complexity to Storm. It’s a story with many dimensions, and one that truly deserves to be singled out amongst an abundance of young adult Paranormals. It’s not one aspect of the story that shines, but a cohesive mix of all its parts, combined to make something layered, something truly unique and special. Storm isn’t about a group of brothers with unbelievable supernatural powers. It’s not about boy meets girl. It’s not about one of the first love triangles I’ve ever read and <em>genuinely enjoyed</em>, nor is it bullying, discrimination, grief or friendship. It’s more. It’s the way in which Kemmerer blends them all together, into a mix of colours more vivid and alluring then any one part could be on its own.<br /><br />Storm is a remarkable debut. Brigid Kemmerer’s gift for characterisation and pitch-perfect voice combine with gripping story and perfect pacing to make Storm a riveting an utterly addictive read. Action packed from start to finish, Brigid’s nailed a perfect balance between excitement, romance and supernatural to create something magic. A story that is so many things, but most importantly, <em>fun</em>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5481247550238284916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_659361625" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659361625" />
    <a title="Irina Elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena"><img alt="Irina Elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587303756p2/7664770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659361625?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irina Elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irina Elena" href="/user/show/7664770-irina-elena">Irina Elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780758280053" href="/book/show/13614844-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=paranormal-or-urban-fantasy">paranormal-or-urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7664770-irina-elena?shelf=ya-pnr">ya-pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659361625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer104758515384318272">Good... good. Very good. Nothing eartshaking, but hey, good is already more than I expected, since I haven't touched a het paranormal YA in months.<br/>It looks like I read it in 8 days, but it was actually 4, with one long break in the middle. This means that no, I wasn't completely sucked in and sitting on the very edge of my seat, but while reading I was mighty interested in what was going to happen next. Good enough.<br/><br/>I was planning on talking at length about all the typically PNR-het-YA stuff that</span>
  <span id="freeText104758515384318272" style="display:none">Good... good. Very good. Nothing eartshaking, but hey, good is already more than I expected, since I haven't touched a het paranormal YA in months.<br />It looks like I read it in 8 days, but it was actually 4, with one long break in the middle. This means that no, I wasn't completely sucked in and sitting on the very edge of my seat, but while reading I was mighty interested in what was going to happen next. Good enough.<br /><br />I was planning on talking at length about all the typically PNR-het-YA stuff that bugged me, but since I've had this review languishing in my brain/to-do list/fingers for ten days what I want right now is honestly to just get rid of it.<br />So: schoolgirl mooning over complete strangers, a love triangle (let's not even), pointless descriptions of clothing, secretly following people around (does anyone actually do that irl? Because it sure happens a lot in books), immediately accepting paranormality but then refusing to trust someone evidently trustworthy just to stick with the mysterious hippie guy (er... yes, I was team Chris. Oh dear. Team? I guess I haven't managed to exterminate my inner schoolgirl completely yet), people who say "crap" (SHIT. <i>Shit</i>. <b>Shit</b>).<br /><br />BUT. There was a lot of good stuff too! Like the fact that all that testosterone was fogging up my phone screen. If I'm reading the next books for one reason, it's the Merrick brothers. I'm sure as hell not interested in the girls. *vaguely disgusted face*<br />I just love the guys' relationship, the way they fight and seem to want to kill each other all the fucking time yet gang up on an enemy or outsider in a second. It might not be the friendliest or most healthy attitude, but it's fantastic to see.<br />btw, I refuse to believe that the guys on the cover are the Merrick brothers. They look like complete tools.<br />Colton Haynes though. Oh god, I'd climb that like a squirrel. (You see? Everything goes back to Teen Wolf.)<br />So Colton Haynes is Chris, in my mind - as if I needed one more reason to want to lick him. Chris, that is. Not that I don't want to lick Colton Haynes. He (Chris) was just too adorable and natural and spontaneous and grumpy and just plain <i>nice</i> to resist. Plus he looks like Colton Haynes. (Humour me.)<br /><br />Hunter, on the other hand, made my brain itch. He was cocky in that "I'm so cool I don't even need to rub it in your face" kinda way that is even worse that straight-out bragging, yet he still had this almost ethereal feel about him that confused me and annoyed me and made my leg automatically jump and kick the table everytime I read his name. If this was the author's intention, kudos; if it wasn't, <i>fix it</i>. Still, I want find out what the hell the deal is with him. One more reason to continue the series, I guess. Also, <i>discoveries</i>! Did you know that hair on a scar grows back white? I had no idea, and when I first read about it here I called bullshit. That's actually kinda cool, anyway.<br /><br />On to Becca - I do have to talk about her, even if I could do without; she's the MC after all. *sigh*<br />Becca was... a girl. As in <i>such a girl</i>. I don't know if I've just lost the ability to like or relate to female characters or authors are just that bad at portraying them, but they end up pissing me off more often than not. Are clothes and boys and the occasional paranormal ability really all we think about? She acted in a moderately logical way though, so I didn't outright despise her. Thank fuck she had some family issues too, at least I could like one thing about her - the way she interacted with the 'rents.<br /><br />The romance was... cheesy, sweet, angsty (in the girly way, which is not angsty at all) but surprisingly okay, because of the good pacing and slow-building tension. Although I can't help but be suprised by the complete absence of actual smut in here - it's like the main characters' hormones are hybernating for some reason. There's an almost-rape (not with one of the love interests, chill!), so the author might not have wanted to put both elements in the same book, but... no, even that doesn't make sense. Whatever.<br /><br />There are some suprises too, if YA lurve and girliness hadn't convinced you to give this a try yet. The double twist at the end took me completely by surprise, despite a couple generous clues dropped during the story. But that's probably just me.<br /><br /><b>tl;dr</b><br />It's het YA paranormal romance.<br />But it's a few steps higher on the originality scale than I expected - and I tend to be pretty optimistic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="104758515384318272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_414469337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/414469337" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/414469337?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414469337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13847995514114018053">In my ongoing quest to improve my life by not finishing stuff I'm editing in my head to be any good, I'm DNFing this at 41%. I hesitate with this one because so many of my friends really liked it (average of 4 stars). And I suppose I can see the appeal, even if I don't feel it, myself.<br/><br/>Hot guys with powers and lots of emotional masculinity and a sympathetic heroine to pilot us around the plot landscape. That's a draw, I have to admit. So why can't I lose myself in a book so many others find engag</span>
  <span id="freeText13847995514114018053" style="display:none">In my ongoing quest to improve my life by not finishing stuff I'm editing in my head to be any good, I'm DNFing this at 41%. I hesitate with this one because so many of my friends really liked it (average of 4 stars). And I suppose I can see the appeal, even if I don't feel it, myself.<br /><br />Hot guys with powers and lots of emotional masculinity and a sympathetic heroine to pilot us around the plot landscape. That's a draw, I have to admit. So why can't I lose myself in a book so many others find engaging?<br /><br />* Too many assholes. I've been trying not to swear as much, but there's no better way to say that. Everybody in this book is a jerk, and I don't just mean the bad guys. This isn't helped by having the chief assholes be the supposed good guys (and no, I do not except Chris, not entirely at any rate).<br />* Becca lives on the edge of sexual assault <em>all the freaking time</em> and nobody seems to be bothered by this. Not even Becca.<br />* The world, once explained (that'll be next), makes no sense whatsoever. I mean, powerful elementals are under an automatic death sentence because they're "too powerful to trust"—said sentence to be carried out by a trained elite cadre of <em>even more powerful elementals</em>? Who thought that made sense?<br />* Holy freaking exposition dump, batman! This is where I broke, actually. You get veiled hints and microscopic pieces of the background (even when in Chris' head) but it's mostly obscured until Chris and Becca get a moment and suddenly he's telling her his life story. This is not only awkward, but breaks my suspension of disbelief. I've been a teen with a complicated backstory to tell possible romantic companions and let me tell you, the best way to ruin any interest that might exist is to dump it all in one go under otherwise sterile circumstances.<br />* The bad guys make no freaking sense, whatsoever. If they truly mean to kill the Merricks (and every evidence points that direction), then why are they faffing about with half-measures and stupid threats all the time? Seems to me that a simple ambush or two would accomplish all they could hope to achieve and heaven knows the Merrick boys are foolish enough to fall for practically anything. Like, just to take a simple example, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[if Tyler has a freaking gun and is willing to use it, then why does he only produce it when it is guaranteed to be ineffective? Seems to me that opening with that little gambit (and while you can actually see your enemy) would have been about fifty times more effective. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />* The good guys make no freaking sense, whatsoever. If a community has been hostile for years with increasing (and increasingly open) violence, then what exactly do you think is going to happen to change that for the better? Denial and appeasement are loser strategies and they're even dumber when you can see, <em>for years</em>, that they <em>aren't working</em>. Let's take the head of the family, Michael. The only person he's willing to confront (with violence, no less) is a lone girl trying to help his brother. Nice call, asshole.<br />* And could Kemmerer be any more awkward in telegraphing Becca's dad's involvement? This is speculation on my part, so this may or may not pan out and be spoilery, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but come on. Dear old dad hasn't been in touch for idunnamany years and suddenly he's trying to get in touch right when the community is set to blow? Becca is just learning about the supernatural, with hints of having her own possible "intuitions" and <em>that's</em> when dear old dad tries to get in touch? Nothing suspicious there... I'm thinking either he or Hunter are the "guide" that's been called in, with the other being there for supernatural reasons of their own—long-lost family or revenge, maybe. Or both <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br />* New boy in town who immediately falls in with Becca. That's not at all suspicious. Not to mention a completely contrived third leg of a stupid love triangle. And then he shows some kind of power on his own, though Becca is conveniently distracted from it because, uh, story.<br /><br />All of that feels harsher than I mean it, really. It's just the list of things I was silently editing in my head. Becca is sweet and her life is enough of a misery that you're pulled in almost immediately. Chris isn't a complete asshole, either, though it helps that we're actually in his head sometimes. You naturally want them to get together because they're the only people even remotely sympathetic (I couldn't buy Hunter as an interest. He was too perfectly placed and had too much enigma attached for me to consider him anything more than a distraction. A contrived distraction, at that). So powers, angst, tension, and violence with a heroine doing her best to navigate troubled waters (both physical and emotional). It's engaging, I admit. But I struggled to get into it and eventually realized it was more effort than I was willing to continue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13847995514114018053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
