<div id="review_311095598" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311095598" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311095598?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780758272812" href="/book/show/10401084-storm">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311095598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14254716647577299532"><br/>The first book in the series, which focus on the Merrick brothers, who each have the power to control a different element. The oldest Michael controls earth, the youngest Chris controls water and the twins Nick and Gabriel control air and fire respectively. <br/>The youngest brother, Chris takes centre stage in Storm. The story starts with Becca Chandler saving Chris from being beaten to death by two guys, outside of her school. Becca soon finds out that no good deed goes unpunished when she's pulled</span>
  <span id="freeText14254716647577299532" style="display:none"><br />The first book in the series, which focus on the Merrick brothers, who each have the power to control a different element. The oldest Michael controls earth, the youngest Chris controls water and the twins Nick and Gabriel control air and fire respectively. <br />The youngest brother, Chris takes centre stage in Storm. The story starts with Becca Chandler saving Chris from being beaten to death by two guys, outside of her school. Becca soon finds out that no good deed goes unpunished when she's pulled into the fight between the Merrick's and the people who want them dead.<br />Chris was a great hero, I always enjoy heroes that aren't sarcastic, cocky, alpha-hole players. Chris has power over water, it was refreshing to see that he wasn't all powerful and all knowing, he was still struggling with his powers and learning control. I found it endearing that Chris was a little nervous and unsure around Becca. I did enjoy his strained relationship with his brother, Micheal, more than his relationship with Becca.<br />The heroine, Becca was kind of blah. I found myself getting irritated with how she didn't stick up for herself more, she also came across as quite Mary Sueish towards the end. I wish they had been more interaction between Becca and her dad, she had more personality around him, whereas with every other character she was quite dull. <br />I thought Becca's best friend Quinn was a far more interesting character, she has a tough home life and relies on Becca for help. I lost a bit of respect for Becca when she pushed Quinn away when it was clear that she needed help. I did notice that the few times Quinn and Nick interacted that there was some sort of vibe between them. Out of the brothers, Nick and Chris were by far the best. I am hoping that Quinn is Nick's heroine. <br />I didn't like that the only male characters that weren't rapey, sexist pigs or complete douche's were Chris and the future love interests of the series. Really author??..that's the only way you can make your heroes swoonworthy and desirable by making all the other male characters villains and bast**ds. <br />What pissed me off the most was the slut shaming that went on in this book. Yes, I'm aware that slut shaming does happen in real life but the extent of slut shaming that certain characters experienced was beyond ridiculous..it felt like I was reading the attitudes and actions of people from the early 1900's. I was really disappointed and angry with one of the brothers attitude, Gabriel, who is a future love interest. He brags about what a player he is and then when he hears that Becca's slept around he talks down to her and acts like she's not worthy to date his brother..so it's ok for him to sleep around but if a girl does it must mean she's evil, dirty, lowlife scum. He only gives his approval to Becca when he finds out that Becca hasn't actually slept around and that it was all just vicious lies. I anticipate that Gabriel will meet some shy, virginal, wide eyed girl that he falls for (because, of course sexually experienced girls aren't good enough for him), he'll stop his playboy ways and live HEA. <br />I did enjoy premise and some of the side characters introduced, I'll probably read how good the reviews are before deciding whether or not to continue with the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14254716647577299532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review311095598">
  <td colspan="2">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Oyec1BTB3Ep7qYKyxD+Wlk85FjLxy4cgCi+xuRC95uSjruG5+t0spI0McwLmkBLx1iEKIfpmqOIMYkdA62PYQQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UHvHmNJxB2skVCLw1A/LO6b65cAwgPjIzTVa849gdTPI8rr1PG33hdLx00D2oE9cP+L50zst1wrLeKwKdL5Llg==')})
  }
//]]>

She\'s got a child of her own, and a job as a firefighter that could put her life in danger at any moment.\n\nBut there are people who have had enough of Michael\'s defiance, his family\'s \'bad luck\'. Before he knows it, Michael\'s enemies have turned into the Merricks\' enemies, and they\'re armed for war.\n\nThey\'re not interested in surrender. But Michael isn\'t the white flag type anyway. Everything is set for the final showdown.\n\nFour elements, one family.   <!--
This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
